<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anatomy">ANATOMY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anatomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Osteology</li>
<li>acetabular inclination &amp; anteversion</li>
<li>mean lateral inclination of 40 to 48 degrees</li>
<li>anteversion of 18 to 21 degrees</li>
<li>column theory</li>
<li>acetabulum is supported by two columns of bone</li>
<li>form an "inverted Y"</li>
<li>connected to sacrum through sciatic buttress</li>
<li>posterior column</li>
<li>comprised of quadrilateral surface</li>
<li>posterior wall and dome</li>
<li>ischial tuberosity</li>
<li>greater/lesser sciatic notches</li>
<li>anterior column</li>
<li>comprised of</li>
<li>anterior ilium (gluteus medius tubercle)</li>
<li>anterior wall and dome</li>
<li>iliopectineal eminence</li>
<li>lateral superior pubic ramus</li>
<li>Vascular</li>
<li>corona mortis</li>
<li>anastomosis of external iliac (epigastric) and internal iliac (obturator)</li>
<li>vessels</li>
<li>at risk with lateral dissection over superior pubic ramus</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="letournel-classification">LETOURNEL CLASSIFICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#letournel-classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Judet and Letournel</li>
<li>most common referenced classification system</li>
<li>classified as 5 elementary and 5 associated fracture patterns</li>
<li>most common fracture patterns</li>
<li>younger</li>
<li>posterior wall</li>
<li>transverse fracture "family"</li>
<li>transverse</li>
</ul>
<p>87</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>T-type
transverse + posterior wall</p>
<p>elderly</p>
<ul>
<li>anterior column (e.g., quadrilateral plate fractures)</li>
<li>anterior column, posterior hemitransverse</li>
<li>associated both column fractures</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260204-def0c4bb.jpeg" alt="img-72.jpeg"></p>
<p>Radiographs</p>
<ul>
<li>Recommended views</li>
<li>AP</li>
<li>judet</li>
</ul>
<p>obturator oblique</p>
<ul>
<li>shows profile of obturator foramen</li>
<li>shows anterior column and posterior wall</li>
</ul>
<p>iliac oblique</p>
<ul>
<li>shows profile of involved iliac wing</li>
<li>shows posterior column and anterior wall</li>
</ul>
<p>Findings</p>
<ul>
<li>radiographic landmarks of the acetabulum</li>
<li>iliopectineal line (anterior column)</li>
<li>ilioischial line (posterior column)</li>
<li>anterior wall</li>
<li>posterior wall</li>
<li>weight bearing roof</li>
</ul>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>Shenton's line</p>
<p>roof arc angle</p>
<ul>
<li>angle between vertical line through femoral head and line through fracture</li>
<li>helps to define fracture pattern stability</li>
<li>considered stable if the fracture line exits outside the weight bearing dome of the acetabulum</li>
<li>defined as &lt; 45 on AP, obturator and iliac oblique views</li>
<li>not applicable for associated both column or posterior wall pattern because no intact portion of the acetabulum to measure</li>
</ul>
<p>gull sign</p>
<ul>
<li>represents impaction of superomedial roof</li>
<li>seen on iliac oblique view</li>
<li>pathognomic for posterior wall fractures</li>
</ul>
<p>spur sign</p>
<ul>
<li>represents most caudal part of intact ilium due to medialization of articular components</li>
<li>seen on obturator oblique view</li>
<li>pathognomic for ABC fractures</li>
</ul>
<p>CT scan</p>
<ul>
<li>oindications</li>
<li>now considered a gold standard in management</li>
<li>ofindings</li>
<li>fracture pattern orientation</li>
<li>define fragment size and orientation</li>
<li>identify marginal impaction</li>
<li>identify loose bodies (e.g., post-reduction)</li>
<li>look for articular gap or step-off</li>
</ul>
<p>Duplex doppler ultrasound</p>
<ul>
<li>oindications</li>
<li>delayed presentation to treating hospital</li>
<li>rule out DVT</li>
</ul>
<p>TREATMENT</p>
<ul>
<li>Nonoperative</li>
<li>oprotected weight bearing for 6-8 weeks</li>
<li>indications</li>
<li>patient factors</li>
<li>high operative risk (e.g., elderly patients, presence of DVT)</li>
<li>morbid obesity</li>
<li>open contaminated wound</li>
<li>late presenting &gt; 3 weeks</li>
<li>fracture characteristics</li>
<li>minimally displaced fracture (&lt; 2 mm)</li>
</ul>
<p>89</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>&lt; 20% posterior wall fractures</p>
<p>treatment based on size of posterior wall is controversial</p>
<p>recommend an exam under anesthesia (EUA) using fluoroscopy best method to test stability</p>
<p>femoral head congruency with weight bearing roof (out of traction)</p>
<p>both column fracture pattern with secondary congruence (out of traction)</p>
<p>displaced fracture with roof arcs &gt; 45 in AP and Judet views or &gt;10 mm on axial CT cuts</p>
<p>technique</p>
<p>skeletal traction NOT required if stable fracture pattern, outside the weight-bearing dome</p>
<p>activity as tolerated with crutches/walker</p>
<p>weight-bearing</p>
<p>lowest joint reactive forces seen with toe-touch weight bearing and passive hip abduction</p>
<p>greatest joint contact force seen when rising from a chair on the affected extremity</p>
<p>DVT prophylaxis</p>
<p>close radiographic follow-up</p>
<p>Operative treatment</p>
<p>oopen reduction and internal fixation</p>
<p>indications</p>
<p>patient factors</p>
<p>&lt; 3 weeks from date of injury</p>
<p>physiologically stable</p>
<p>adequate soft-tissue envelope</p>
<p>no local infection</p>
<p>pregnancy is not contraindication to surgical fixation</p>
<p>fracture factors</p>
<p>displacement of roof (&gt; 2 mm)</p>
<p>unstable fracture pattern (e.g. posterior wall fracture involving &gt; 40-50%)</p>
<p>marginal impaction</p>
<p>intra-articular loose bodies</p>
<p>irreducible fracture-dislocation</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>total hip arthroplasty</p>
<p>indications</p>
<ul>
<li>usually elderly patients with</li>
<li>significant osteopenia and/or significant comminution</li>
<li>pre-existing arthritis</li>
<li>post-traumatic arthritis in all ages</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">COMPLICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Post-traumatic Degenerative Joint Disease</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>most common complication</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>80% survival noted at 20 years for patients s/p ORIF</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>risk factors for DJD include</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>age &gt;40</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>associated fracture patterns</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>concomitant femoral head injury</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Heterotopic ossification</p>
<ul>
<li>Osteonecrosis</li>
<li>DVT and PE</li>
<li>Infection</li>
<li>Bleeding</li>
<li>Neurovascular injury</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prognosis">PROGNOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prognosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Poor outcomes are associated with:</li>
<li>multi-system trauma</li>
<li>increasing age</li>
<li>poor articular congruency</li>
<li>associated femoral head articular injury</li>
<li>post-traumatic arthritis</li>
</ul>
<p>91</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hip-dislocation-fracture">HIP DISLOCATION +_ fracture:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hip-dislocation-fracture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="learning-objectives">LEARNING OBJECTIVES:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Classify dislocations and fracture-dislocations of the hip</li>
<li>State the precautions you take in order not to miss the diagnosis of hip injury</li>
<li>Describe the mode of injury of posterior dislocation of the hip</li>
<li>Describe the clinical features of posterior dislocation/fracture-dislocation of the hip</li>
<li>Describe the treatment of posterior dislocation of the hip</li>
<li>State the complications of posterior dislocation/fracture-dislocation of the hip</li>
<li>Describe the mode of injury of anterior dislocation of the hip</li>
<li>Describe the clinical features of anterior dislocation of the hip</li>
<li>Describe the treatment of anterior dislocation of the hip</li>
<li>State the complications of anterior dislocation of the hip.</li>
<li>Describe central fracture-dislocation of the hip</li>
<li>Describe the mode of injury of central fracture dislocation of the hip</li>
<li>Describe the treatment of central fracture-dislocation of the hip</li>
<li>Outline the complications of central fracture-dislocation of the hip</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">INTRODUCTION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hip dislocations are traumatic hip injuries that result in femoral head dislocation from the acetabular socket.</li>
<li>Diagnosis can be made with hip radiographs to determine the direction of dislocation and CT scan studies to assess for associated injuries.</li>
<li>Treatment is urgent reduction to minimize risk of avascular necrosis followed by CT scan to assess for associated injuries that may require surgical treatment (loose bodies, femoral head fractures, acetabular fractures).</li>
</ul>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification">CLASSIFICATION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hip dislocations are classified based on
(1) the relationship of the femoral head to the acetabulum
(2) whether or not associated fractures are present.</p>
<p>3 main types:</p>
<ul>
<li>Posterior dislocation or fracture-dislocation</li>
<li>Anterior dislocation</li>
<li>Central fracture-dislocation.</li>
</ul>
<p>Posterior dislocation is the commonest.</p>
<p>When there are other serious injuries in the same limb, particularly a fracture of the shaft of the femur, it is easy to overlook a dislocation or fracture-dislocation of the hip.</p>
<p>Do a full clinical survey of the whole body in cases of major injury</p>
<p>Make sure the X-rays in every case of fractured femoral shaft take in the whole length of the bone and include the hip joint.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="posterior-dislocation">POSTERIOR DISLOCATION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#posterior-dislocation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Posterior Dislocations comprise 85% to 90% of traumatic hip dislocations.</p>
<p>Mode of injury</p>
<ul>
<li>The femoral head is forced out of the back of the acetabulum by violence applied along the shaft of femur while the hip is flexed or semi flexed.</li>
<li>E.g., motor vehicle accident  car involved in collision- occupant thrown forwards and strikes the front of his flexed knees against a part of the vehicle body framework (e.g., dashboard injury)</li>
<li>Motor cycle accident</li>
</ul>
<p>About  of the cases are fracture-dislocations; the head of femur carries with it a fragment of bone from the rim of the acetabulum.</p>
<p>If the hip is in the neutral or slightly adducted position at the time of impact, a dislocation without acetabular fracture will likely occur.</p>
<p>If the hip is in slight abduction, an associated fracture of the posterior-superior rim of the acetabulum usually occurs.</p>
<p>Unrestrained motor vehicle accident occupants are at a significantly higher risk for sustaining a hip dislocation than passengers wearing a restraining device.</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260204-9e00d2c5.jpeg" alt="img-73.jpeg">
CLINICAL PRACTICE</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260204-14042b79.jpeg" alt="img-74.jpeg"></p>
<p>Pain in the affected hip
Inability to use the limb
Medial rotation of the femur and whole lower limb
Upward displacement of femur leading to shortening of the limb by 2-3 cm.
Adduction of the femur (thigh)
Flexion of the hip and knee
*examine for signs of sciatic nerve injury</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="investigations">INVESTIGATIONS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>X-ray of the pelvis A/P view will show the dislocation. Upward, outward and posterior displacement.
If there is an associated acetabular fracture it will be shown.
The femur is seen medially rotated and adducted</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260204-f08dbf6d.jpeg" alt="img-75.jpeg"></p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">TREATMENT:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Reduction under general anaesthesia as soon as possible by pulling longitudinally upon the femur while the hip is flexed at right angle and rotated laterally.</p>
<p>Technique:</p>
<p>Patient is placed supine on the floor or on a low table, and an assistant grasps the pelvis firmly through the iliac crests. You then flex the hip and knee to right angle so that the line of the femur points vertically upwards. You then pull the thigh steadily upwards, at the same time gradually rotating the femur laterally.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="allis-method-of-reduction">ALLIS METHOD OF REDUCTION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#allis-method-of-reduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This consists of traction applied in line with the deformity.</p>
<p>The patient is placed supine with the surgeon standing above the patient on the stretcher or table.</p>
<p>Initially, the surgeon applies in-line traction while the assistant applies countertraction by stabilizing the patient's pelvis.</p>
<p>While increasing the traction force, the surgeon should slowly increase the degree of flexion to approximately 70 degrees.</p>
<p>Gentle rotational motions of the hip as well as slight adduction will often help the femoral head to clear the lip of the acetabulum.</p>
<p>A lateral force to the proximal thigh may assist in reduction.</p>
<p>An audible "clunk" is a sign of a successful closed reduction</p>
<p>After reduction, a light skin traction (Russell's) is applied for 3 weeks.</p>
<p>Meanwhile, mobilizing exercises for the hip and knee are begun after a few days and are gradually intensified.</p>
<p>A small marginal fragment from the acetabulum usually falls back into place following reduction of the dislocation.</p>
<p>If a large acetabular fragment remains unreduced, open reduction and internal fixation with a screw or small plate is required.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="operative-treatment">OPERATIVE TREATMENT:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#operative-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Indications for open reduction of a dislocated hip include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Dislocation irreducible by closed means</li>
<li>Nonconcentric reduction</li>
<li>Fracture of the acetabulum or femoral head requiring excision or open reduction and internal fixation</li>
<li>Ipsilateral femoral neck fracture</li>
</ul>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">COMPLICATIONS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Injury to the sciatic nerve</li>
<li>Damage to the femoral head</li>
<li>Avascular necrosis of the femoral head</li>
<li>Post-traumatic ossification</li>
<li>Osteoarthritis</li>
<li>Recurrent dislocation</li>
<li>Unreduced dislocation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="injury-to-sciatic-nerve">Injury to sciatic nerve:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#injury-to-sciatic-nerve" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sciatic nerve lies behind the posterior wall of the acetabulum and is vulnerable to injury. It is particularly liable to damage when a large acetabular wall fragment is driven backwards with the head of femur.</p>
<p>The nerve lesion is usually a neurapraxia or an axonotmesis, but it may be virtually a complete division (neurotmesis).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Relief of pressure by early reduction of dislocation and replacement of displaced bone fragment, if possible, by operation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prognosis">Prognosis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prognosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Good after minor nerve lesion (neurapraxia)</li>
<li>Poor after severe injury of the nerve at this high level. Recovery of good muscle power is poor because of the length to be regenerated and the likelihood that the distal muscles will have suffered irreversible changes before they are reinnervated.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="thompson-and-epstein-classification-of-posterior-hip-dislocations">Thompson and Epstein Classification of Posterior Hip Dislocations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thompson-and-epstein-classification-of-posterior-hip-dislocations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Type I: Simple dislocation with or without an insignificant posterior wall fragment</li>
<li>Type II: Dislocation associated with a single large posterior wall fragment</li>
<li>Type III: Dislocation with a comminuted posterior wall fragment</li>
<li>Type IV: Dislocation with fracture of the acetabular floor</li>
<li>Type V: Dislocation with fracture of the femoral head</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Post-traumatic arthritis</li>
<li>up to 20% for simple dislocation, markedly increased for complex dislocation</li>
</ul>
<p>96</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>oFemoral head osteonecrosis
5-40% incidence
Increased risk with increased time to reduction</p>
<p>oSciatic nerve injury
8-20% incidence
associated with longer time to reduction</p>
<p>oRecurrent dislocations
less than 2%</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="anterior-dislocation-of-the-hip">Anterior dislocation of the Hip:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anterior-dislocation-of-the-hip" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Less common than posterior dislocation
Caused by forced abduction and lateral rotation of the limb, usually in a violent injury
e.g., motor accident or aircraft crash.
Usually no associated acetabular fracture.
These injuries result from external rotation and abduction of the hip.
The degree of hip flexion determines whether a superior or inferior type of anterior hip dislocation results.
Inferior (obturator) dislocation is the result of simultaneous abduction, external rotation, and hip flexion.
Superior (iliac or pubic) dislocation is the result of simultaneous abduction, external rotation, and hip extension.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260204-a3fee478.jpeg" alt="img-76.jpeg">
Clinical features:</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>Pain in the hip
Inability to use the limb
Tenderness in the hip region
Hip is in extension
Limb rests in marked lateral rotation
Abduction of the hip</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Reduction under anaesthesia
By strong traction upon the limb combined with medial rotation.
Apply light skin traction for 3-4 weeks</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rarely, injury to the femoral artery, vein, or nerve may occur as a result of an anterior dislocation.
Avascular necrosis
Osteoarthritis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="epstein-classification-of-anterior-hip-dislocations">Epstein Classification of Anterior Hip Dislocations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#epstein-classification-of-anterior-hip-dislocations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Type I: Superior dislocations, including pubic and subspinous
IA: No associated fractures
IB: Associated fracture or impaction of the femoral head
IC: Associated fracture of the acetabulum</p>
<p>Type II: Inferior dislocations, including obturator, and perineal
IIA: No associated fractures
IIB: Associated fracture or impaction of the femoral head
IIC: Associated fracture of the acetabulum</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="central-fracture-dislocation">Central Fracture-dislocation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#central-fracture-dislocation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The femoral head is driven through the medial wall, or 'floor', of the acetabulum towards the pelvic cavity.
The capsule remains intact, but
There is inevitably a fracture of the acetabulum, usually with much comminution.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Central fracture-dislocation is caused by a heavy lateral blow upon the femur as occurs in a fall from a height on to the side.</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>A longitudinal force acting upon the femur (e.g. a blow upon a flexed knee) while the hip is abducted</p>
<p>Degree of displacement:</p>
<p>Depends on the severity of the violence / force</p>
<p>Minor type:</p>
<p>Fracture of the acetabulum with only minimal inwards displacement (a few millimeters)</p>
<p>Severe type:</p>
<p>The innominate bone, including the acetabulum, is shattered and driven inwards together with the femoral head (protrusion acetabula)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260204-ec0181d2.jpeg" alt="img-77.jpeg"></p>
<p>Energetic resuscitation if shocked / internal bleeding</p>
<p>Treatment depends largely upon the degree of comminution and displacement of the acetabular fragments, and upon whether or not it is possible to restore the articular surface to its normal shape.</p>
<p>Cases in which restoration of the articular surface is possible:</p>
<p>If the major part of the weight-bearing area of the acetabulum remains mainly in one piece, attempt to restore it to its anatomical position.</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>Apply heavy weight traction upon the femur through a Steinmann pin passed antero-posteriorly through the greater trochanter. The direction of pull should be downwards and outwards.</p>
<p>After reduction, maintain traction (light) for 4-6 weeks</p>
<p>If traction fails, the fragment can be reduced at operation and fixed with screws and contoured plates, then maintained on light traction for 4-6 weeks.</p>
<p>Cases in which severe comminution precludes accurate reduction:</p>
<p>Reduce the femoral head to the normal position in the acetabulum by applying combined lateral and downward traction through pins transfixing the trochanter and the lower end of femur.</p>
<p>Duration of traction: 6 weeks</p>
<p>Complications:</p>
<p>Severe haemorrhage from damage to major blood vessel</p>
<p>Osteoarthritis  treated by arthrodesis or total hip replacement.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fracture-head-femur">FRACTURE HEAD FEMUR:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fracture-head-femur" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Femoral head fractures are rare traumatic injuries that are usually associated with hip dislocations.</p>
<p>Diagnosis can be made by pelvis/hip radiographs but frequently require CT scan for surgical planning.</p>
<p>Treatment may be nonoperative or operative depending on the location of the fracture and degree of fracture displacement.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="etiology">ETIOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi></mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.0037em;"></span></span></span></span></span> Pathophysiology</p>
<p>mechanism of injury</p>
<p>impaction, avulsion or shear forces involved</p>
<p>unrestrained passenger MVA (knee against dashboard)</p>
<p>falls from height</p>
<p>sports injury</p>
<p>industrial accidents</p>
<p>pathoanatomy</p>
<p>the location and size of the fracture fragment and degree of</p>
<p>comminution depend on the position of the hip at the time of dislocation</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>5-15% of posterior hip dislocations are associated with a
femoral head fracture because of contact between femoral head and posterior rim of acetabulum
anterior hip dislocations are associated
with impaction/indentation fractures of the femoral head</p>
<p>oAssociated conditions
femoral neck fracture
acetabular fracture
sciatic nerve neuropraxia
femoral head AVN
ipsilateral knee ligamentous instability (knee vs dashboard)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anatomy">ANATOMY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anatomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>oBlood supply
medial femoral circumflex artery (MFCA)
main blood supply to the weightbearing portion of the femoral head
MFCA originates from the profunda femoris
artery to the ligamentum teres
lesser blood supply (10-15%)
from the obturator artery or MFCA
supplies perifoveal area</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification">CLASSIFICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>oPipkin Classification</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>oFracture below fovea/ ligamentum (small)</th><th></th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>oType I</td><td>oDoes not involve the weight-bearing portion of the femoral head</td><td>o</td></tr><tr><td>oType II</td><td>oFracture above fovea/ ligamentum (larger)</td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td>oInvolves the weight-bearing portion of the femoral head</td><td>o</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>oType I or II with an associated femoral neck fracture</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>oType III</td><td>oHigh incidence of AVN</td><td>o</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>oType I or II with associated acetabular fx (usually</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>oType IV</td><td>posterior wall fracture)</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="presentation">PRESENTATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>oHistory</p>
<ul>
<li>frontal impact MVA with knee striking dashboard</li>
<li>fall from height</li>
</ul>
<p>oSymptoms</p>
<ul>
<li>localized hip pain</li>
<li>unable to bear weight</li>
<li>other symptoms associated with impact</li>
</ul>
<p>oPhysical exam</p>
<ul>
<li>inspection</li>
<li>shortened lower limb</li>
<li>with large acetabular wall fractures, little to no rotational asymmetry is seen</li>
<li>posterior dislocation</li>
<li>limb is flexed, abducted, internally rotated</li>
<li>anterior dislocation</li>
<li>limb is flexed, abducted, externally rotated</li>
<li>ipsilateral knee</li>
<li>ligamentous stability</li>
</ul>
<p>neurovascular</p>
<ul>
<li>may have signs of sciatic nerve injury</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="investigations">investigations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>x-ray ap/lateral /jedet confirms the diagnosis.</p>
<p>Radiographs</p>
<ul>
<li>orecommended views</li>
<li>AP pelvis, hip series</li>
<li>both pre-reduction and post-reduction</li>
<li>judet views</li>
<li>associated acetabular fracture</li>
<li>inlet and outlet views</li>
<li>associated pelvic ring injury</li>
</ul>
<p>CT scan</p>
<ul>
<li>indications</li>
<li>opost reduction to evaluate for loose bodies and presence/size of fracture fragments</li>
</ul>
<p>TREATMENT</p>
<ul>
<li>Nonoperative</li>
<li>ohip reduction</li>
<li>indications</li>
<li>acute dislocations</li>
<li>reduce hip dislocation within 6 hours</li>
<li>outcomes</li>
<li>5-40% incidence of femoral head osteonecrosis</li>
<li>increased risk with increased time to reduction</li>
</ul>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>o(touch down weight bearing)TDWB x 4-6 weeks, restrict adduction and internal rotation</p>
<p>indications</p>
<ul>
<li>Pipkin I</li>
<li>nondisplaced Pipkin II with &lt; 1 mm step off</li>
<li>no interposed fragments</li>
<li>stable hip joint</li>
</ul>
<p>outcomes</p>
<ul>
<li>serial radiographs required</li>
<li>development of post-traumatic arthritis based on joint incongruity and initial cartilage damage</li>
</ul>
<p>Operative</p>
<p>ORIF</p>
<p>oindications</p>
<ul>
<li>Pipkin II with &gt; 1 mm step off</li>
<li>if performing removal of loose bodies in the joint</li>
<li>associated neck or acetabular fx (Pipkin type III and IV)</li>
<li>polytrauma</li>
<li>irreducible fracture-dislocation</li>
<li>Pipkin IV</li>
<li>treatment dictated by characteristics of acetabular fracture</li>
<li>small posterior wall fragments can be treated nonsurgically and suprafoveal fractures can then be treated through an anterior approach</li>
</ul>
<p>arthroplasty</p>
<p>oindications</p>
<ul>
<li>Pipkin I, II (displaced), III, and IV in older patients</li>
<li>fractures that are significantly displaced, osteoporotic or comminuted</li>
</ul>
<p>ooutcomes</p>
<ul>
<li>best resereved for older patients</li>
<li>higher dislocation risk than Total Hip Arthroplasty performed for OA</li>
</ul>
<p>arthroscopy</p>
<p>oindications</p>
<ul>
<li>removal of loose bodies</li>
</ul>
<p>ooutcomes</p>
<ul>
<li>dependent on ability to remove incarcerated fragments and initial cartilage damage</li>
</ul>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>rehabilitation</p>
<ul>
<li>mobilization</li>
<li>immediate early range of motion</li>
<li>weightbearing</li>
<li>delay weight bearing for 6-8 weeks</li>
<li>stress strengthening of the quadriceps and abductors</li>
<li>radiographs</li>
<li>radiographs after 6 months to evaluate for AVN and osteoarthritis</li>
</ul>
<p>COMPLICATIONS</p>
<ul>
<li>Heterotopic ossification</li>
<li>AVN</li>
<li>incidence is 0-23%</li>
<li>risk is greater with delayed reduction of dislocated hip</li>
<li>Sciatic nerve neuropraxia</li>
<li>incidence is 10-23%</li>
<li>usually peroneal division of sciatic nerve spontaneous recovery of function in 60-70%</li>
<li>DJD (degenerative joint disease)</li>
<li>incidence 8-75%</li>
<li>due to joint incongruity or initial cartilage damage</li>
<li>Decreased internal rotation</li>
<li>may not be clinically problematic or cause disability</li>
<li>unreduced dislocation</li>
<li>Recurrent instability</li>
</ul>
<p>104</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="neck-femur-fracture">NECK FEMUR FRACTURE:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neck-femur-fracture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Femoral neck fractures are common injuries to the proximal femur associated with increased risk of avascular necrosis, and high levels of patient morbidity and mortality.</p>
<p>Diagnosis is generally made radiographically with orthogonal radiographs of the hip.</p>
<p>Treatment is generally operative with open reduction and internal fixation versus arthroplasty depending on the age of the patient, activity demands and pre-injury mobility.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="epidemiology">EPIDEMIOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#epidemiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Incidence</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi></mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.0037em;"></span></span></span></span></span> common</p>
<p>increasingly common due to aging population</p>
<p>Demographics</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi></mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.0037em;"></span></span></span></span></span> women &gt; men</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="etiology">ETIOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi></mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.0037em;"></span></span></span></span></span> Pathophysiology</p>
<p>healing potential</p>
<p>femoral neck is intracapsular, bathed in synovial fluid</p>
<p>lacks periosteal layer</p>
<p>callus formation limited, which affects healing</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi></mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.0037em;"></span></span></span></span></span> Mechanism</p>
<p>high energy in young patients</p>
<p>low energy falls in older patients</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo></mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\circ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord"></span></span></span></span></span> Associated injuries</p>
<p>femoral shaft fractures</p>
<p>6-9% associated with femoral neck fractures</p>
<p>treat femoral neck first followed by shaft</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anatomy">ANATOMY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anatomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Osteology</p>
<p>onormal neck shaft-angle 130 +/- 7 degrees
onormal anteversion 10 +/- 7 degrees</p>
<p>Blood supply to femoral head</p>
<p>o major contributor is medial femoral circumflex (lateral epiphyseal artery)
osome contribution to anterior and inferior head from lateral femoral circumflex
osome contribution from inferior gluteal artery
osmall and insignificant supply from artery of ligamentum teres
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo></mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\circ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord"></span></span></span></span></span> displacement of femoral neck fracture will disrupt the blood supply and cause an intracapsular hematoma.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification">CLASSIFICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Garden Classification</p>
<p>(based on AP radiographs and does not consider lateral or</p>
<p>sagittal plane alignment)</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Type I Incomplete fx (valgus impacted)</th><th></th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Type II</td><td>Complete fx, nondisplaced</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Type III</td><td>Complete fx, partially displaced</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Type IV</td><td>Complete fx, fully displaced</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Simplified Garden Classification</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Nondisplaced</th><th>Includes Garden I and II</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Displaced</td><td>Includes Garden III and IV</td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Pauwels Classification</p>
<p>(based on vertical orientation of fracture line)</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Type I</th><th>&lt; 30 deg from horizontal</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Type II</td><td>30 to 50 deg from horizontal</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Type</td><td>&gt; 50 deg from horizontal (most unstable</td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>III</p>
<p>with highest risk of nonunion/AVN)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anatomical-classification">ANATOMICAL CLASSIFICATION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anatomical-classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are three types:</p>
<p>subcapital: femoral head/neck junction.</p>
<p>transcervical: midportion of femoral neck.</p>
<p>basicervical: base of femoral neck.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260204-6a3515e8.jpeg" alt="img-78.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment">TREATMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Nonoperative</p>
<p>observation alone</p>
<p>indications</p>
<p>may be considered in some patients who are non-ambulators, have minimal pain, and who are at high risk for surgical intervention</p>
<p>skin traction for 6weeks.</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Operative</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>ORIF</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>indications</td><td>displaced fractures in young or physiologically young patients</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>ORIF indicated for most pts &lt;50 years of age</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>female sex associated with increased reoperation rate</td></tr><tr><td>cannulated screw fixation</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>indications</td><td>nondisplaced transcervical fx</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Garden I or II in the physiologically elderly</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>displaced transcervical fx in young patient</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>achieve reduction to limit vascular insult</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>reduction must be anatomic, so open if necessary</td></tr><tr><td>sliding hip screw</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>indications</td><td>basicervical fracture</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>vertical fracture pattern in a young patient</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>sliding hip screw biomechanically superior to cannulated screws (may not be clinically superior)</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>consider placement of additional cannulated screw above sliding hip screw to prevent rotation</td></tr><tr><td>hemiarthroplasty</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>indications</td><td>debilitated elderly patients</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>metabolic bone disease</td></tr><tr><td>cemented hemiarthroplasty</td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td>decreased fracture rates</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>improved short- and medium-term mobility</td></tr><tr><td>total hip arthroplasty</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>indications</td><td>older active patients</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>patients with preexisting hip osteoarthritis
more predictable pain relief and better functional outcome than hemiarthroplasty
Garden III or IV in patient &lt; 85 years</p>
<p>COMPLICATIONS
oOsteonecrosis (AVN)
oNonunion
oFailure rates
oLoss of independence
oHip osteoarthritis
oMalunion
odislocation</p>
<p>FRACTURES OF TROCHANTERIC REGION:
These are fractures lying in the region between the greater and lesser trochanter.
Trochanteric fractures unite readily no matter how they are treated.
Avascular necrosis and non-union are hardly encountered.
Common in the elderly- especially in women.
The cause is nearly always a fall.
Intertrochanteric Fractures are common extracapsular fractures of the proximal femur at the level of the greater and lesser trochanter that are most commonly seen following ground-level falls in the elderly population.
Diagnosis is made with orthogonal radiographs of the hip. MRI is most helpful to evaluate occult hip fractures.
Treatment is generally operative with sliding hip screw versus cephalomedullary nail depending on fracture stability.</p>
<p>Risk factors
oproximal humerus fractures increase risk of hip fracture for 1 year
oosteoporosis
oadvancing age
oincreased number of comorbidities
oincreased dependency with ADLs</p>
<p>CLINICAL FEATURES:
History of fall
Unable to get up without assistance
Unable to put weight on the limb
Severe pain in trochanteric region
Swelling</p>
<p>O/E:</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>Lateral rotation of the limb
Shortening of the limb
Marked tenderness over trochanteric region
Visible ecchymosis at back of upper thigh (a feature not seen in case of femoral neck # coz extravasated blood is retained within joint capsule)</p>
<p>Blood supply
rich collateral circulation reduces risk of nonunion
trochanteric anastomosis
ascending branch of medial circumflex femoral artery (MFCA)
ascending branch of lateral circumflex femoral artery (LFCA)
deep branch of superior gluteal artery
inferior gluteal artery
transverse branch of LFCA and MFCA
periosteum and surrounding muscles</p>
<p>RADIOGRAPHIC EXAMINATION:</p>
<p>Anteroposterior and lateral radiographs are required.
In most cases the fracture is obvious
A fracture without displacement may easily be overlooked
Careful scrutiny of the radiographs is necessary.</p>
<p>CLASSIFICATION:</p>
<p>Classified into 4 types:
Type 1: undisplaced, uncomminuted fracture
Type 2: displaced; minimal comminution; lesser trochanter fracture; varus deformity.
Type 3: displaced fracture; greater trochanter fractured; comminution; varus deformity.
Type 4: severely comminuted; subtrochanteric extension of fracture.</p>
<p>TREATMENT:</p>
<p>Trochanteric fractures heal readily.
Fragments should be held in good position
Early internal fixation is the treatment of choice in elderly patients.</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>Internal fixation is by a compression screw-plate (dynamic hip screw)</p>
<p>Post-op. the patient is nursed free in bed with active hip and knee exercises from the start.</p>
<p>Walking with partial support of a walking frame or crutches is begun within 1 or 2 days of operation.</p>
<p>Continuous traction:</p>
<p>In young patients, conservative treatment by rest in bed with continuous weight traction can be used with good results.</p>
<p>Russells traction is very suitable for these cases.</p>
<p>Traction is maintained for 10-12 weeks.</p>
<p>Plaster hip spica:</p>
<p>May be used to immobilize the fracture in children after manipulative reduction.</p>
<p>COMPLICATIONS:</p>
<p>Failure of the fixation device  the fixation screw may cut out from the femoral head if the bone is very soft (osteoporosis), especially in severe comminution.</p>
<p>Mal-union  is a frequent complication of trochanteric fractures. Union with reduced neck-shaft angle (coxa vara) is common. Marked lateral rotation of the shaft fragment may occur in neglected cases.</p>
<p>Coxa vara is associated with shortening, but this seldom exceeds 2 or 3 cm</p>
<p>Intertrochanteric femur fracture</p>
<p>111</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260204-0dea8a7d.jpeg" alt="img-79.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fractures-shaft-of-femur">FRACTURES SHAFT OF FEMUR:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fractures-shaft-of-femur" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><del>Femoral shaft fractures are high energy injuries to the femur that are associated with life-threatening injuries (pulmonary, cerebral) and ipsilateral femoral neck fractures.</del></p>
<p>Diagnosis is made radiographically with radiographs of the femur as well as the hip to rule out ipsilateral femoral neck fractures.</p>
<p>Treatment generally involves intramedullary nailing which is associated with &gt;95% union rates.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="etiology">ETIOLOGY:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Mechanism</p>
<ul>
<li>otraumatic</li>
<li>high-energy</li>
<li>most common in younger population</li>
<li>often a result of high-speed motor vehicle accidents</li>
<li>low-energy</li>
</ul>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>more common in elderly
often a result of a fall from standing
gunshot</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification">CLASSIFICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>0</p>
<p>Winquist and Hansen Classification</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Type 0</th><th>No comminution</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Type I</td><td>Insignificant amount of comminution</td></tr><tr><td>Type II</td><td>Greater than 50% cortical contact</td></tr><tr><td>Type III</td><td>Less than 50% cortical contact</td></tr><tr><td>Type IV</td><td>Segmental fracture with no contact between proximal and distal fragment</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>AO/OTA Classification</p>
<table><thead><tr><th></th><th>A1 - Spiral</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>32A -</td><td>A2 - Oblique, angle &gt; 30 degrees</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Simple</td><td>A3 - Transverse, angle &lt; 30 degrees</td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td>B1 - Spiral wedge</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>32B -</td><td>B2 - Bending wedge</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Wedge</td><td>B3 - Fragmented wedge</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>32C -</td><td>C1 - Spiral</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Comple</td><td>C2 - Segmental</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>x</td><td>C3 - Irregula</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Occurs at any age</p>
<p>Almost equally common in the upper, middle and lower thirds</p>
<p>Follows severe violence e.g. RTA, fall from a height, trauma by heavy object.</p>
<p>Upper third is common site for pathological fracture due to carcinomatous metastasis</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="patterns">PATTERNS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patterns" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Transverse</li>
<li>Oblique</li>
<li>Spiral</li>
<li>Comminuted</li>
<li>Greenstick (children)</li>
<li>Segmental</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260204-a60e79a6.jpeg" alt="img-80.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clical-features">CLICAL FEATURES:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Severe pain over the thigh</li>
<li>Swelling</li>
<li>Deformity</li>
<li>Lateral rotation of leg</li>
<li>Marked tenderness over the thigh</li>
<li>Shortening of the limb</li>
<li>Mobility may be demonstrable at mid-thigh</li>
<li>Bone feels thickened due to overlapped fragments</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="radiographic-examination">RADIOGRAPHIC EXAMINATION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#radiographic-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Should always take in the hip and knee</li>
<li>Likelihood of overlooking hip dislocation in fracture of femoral shaft if hip not captured on X-ray.</li>
<li>X-rays will show the position and type of fracture, and also any displacement.</li>
<li>Displacement may be marked, in the form of angulation and overlap.</li>
</ul>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">TREATMENT:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Conservative treatment by sustained traction</li>
<li>Operative treatment:</li>
<li>Internal fixation</li>
<li>External fixation</li>
<li>Gallows or Bryants traction in children below 3 years</li>
<li>Conservative treatment by sustained traction</li>
<li>Reduce the fracture by traction or manipulation</li>
<li>Support the limb in a Thomass splint</li>
<li>Maintain continuous traction by means of a weight</li>
<li>Rehabilitation by exercise</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reduction">REDUCTION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Traction to lower leg by either skin or skeletal traction</li>
<li>A Thomass splint with Pearson knee flexion attachment is fitted.</li>
<li>By combination of traction and manipulation an attempt is made to bring the fragments into correct apposition and alignment.</li>
<li>Canvas strips slung between the bars of the Thomass splint are adjusted for tension</li>
<li>The knee is flexed 15 or 20 degrees to permit control of rotation.</li>
<li>Weight of 4-6kg (10-15 pounds) is attached to traction cord according to build of patient.</li>
<li>Repeat check X-rays are advisable in the first 2 weeks and appropriate adjustments to the slings or weight made as required.</li>
<li>Traction is maintained for 12-16 weeks in adults</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rehabilitation">REHABILITATION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rehabilitation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Exercises for the lower leg and foot to preserve muscle tone and prevent deformity (equinus)</li>
<li>Active quadriceps and knee exercises are begun as soon as initial pain of fracture wanes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="operative-treatment-internal-fixation">OPERATIVE TREATMENT INTERNAL FIXATION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#operative-treatment-internal-fixation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Intramedullary nail</li>
<li>Plain intramedullary nail (e.g. Kunstcher nail)</li>
<li>Perforated nail with locking screws (interlocking nail e.g. Sign nail)  enhances fixation and controls rotation.</li>
<li>Postoperatively the patient lies free in bed and exercises the hip, knee and related muscles.</li>
<li>Walking with partial support of crutches is begun 2 or 3 weeks after operation</li>
<li>Plate and screws</li>
<li>Is used where the medullary cavity is too wide for nail</li>
</ul>
<p>115</p>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p>Can be used as an alternative method to nailing</p>
<p>Need at least 4 holes for fixation of the plate above the fracture and 4 holes below the fracture.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gallows-bryants-traction">GALLOWS / BRYANTS TRACTION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gallows-bryants-traction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>For children up to 3 years old</p>
<ul>
<li>The child's lower limbs are suspended from an overhead beam by means of adhesive skin strapping applied directly to the legs.</li>
<li>The cords are tightened just enough to raise child's buttock clear of the mattress</li>
<li>The weight of the pelvis and lower trunk provides reduction and alignment.</li>
<li>Traction is maintained for 3-4 weeks</li>
<li>Knees should be semi-flexed by splints to prevent spasm of a major artery.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">COMPLICATIONS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Simultaneous dislocation of the hip</li>
<li>Injury to major artery (femoral artery)</li>
<li>Injury to nerve (sciatic nerve, tibial nerve, common peroneal nerve)</li>
<li>Infection (for open fracture)</li>
<li>Delayed union (insufficient union after 5 months)</li>
<li>Non-union (no union. # surfaces rounded and sclerotic)</li>
<li>Mal-union (angulation, overlap  shortening, lateral bowing)</li>
<li>Stiffness of the knee (periarticular and intramuscular adhesions)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="supracondylar-fracture-of-the-femur">SUPRACONDYLAR FRACTURE OF THE FEMUR:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supracondylar-fracture-of-the-femur" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Distal femur fractures are traumatic injuries involving the region extending from the distal metaphyseal-diaphyseal junction to the articular surface of the femoral condyles.</li>
<li>Diagnosis is made radiographically with CT studies often required to assess for intra-articular extension.</li>
<li>Treatment is generally operative with ORIF, intramedullary nail, or distal femur replacement depending on available bone stock, age of patient, and patient activity demands.</li>
</ul>
<p>TRAUMATOLOGY TWO. (COTM)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260204-0cdf1519.jpeg" alt="img-81.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="features">FEATURES:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Occurs just proximal to the point where the medial and lateral cortices of the femur flare out to form the condyles.</p>
<p>May be T-shaped # line due to vertical extension of the fracture split <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi mathvariant="normal">Y</mi><mo></mo></mover></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\dot{\mathrm{Y}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.9202em;"></span><span class="mord accent"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.9202em;"><span style="top: -3em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.025em;">Y</span></span><span style="top: -3.2523em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="accent-body" style="left: -0.1389em;"><span class="mord"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> ng the condyles apart.</p>
<p>The main fracture is more or less transverse</p>
<p>The distal fragment is commonly tilted anteriorly upon the shaft, without serious loss of end-to-end apposition.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification">CLASSIFICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Descriptive</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>supracondylar</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>intercondylar</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>oOTA: 33</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A: extraarticular</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>B: partial articular</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>portion of the articular surface remains in continuity with shaft</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>33B3 is in the coronal plane (Hoffa fragment)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>C: complete articular</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>articular fragment separated from the shaft</p>
</li>
</ul>
